1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)

file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

{"content":"1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference pa

73-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive migration guide for the Envoy External Processing filter from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0. Here's what I've documented:

## Summary of Changes Found

### **Breaking Changes:**
1. **ImmediateResponse.body type change**: `string` → `bytes` - This requires regenerating protobuf code in external processors
2. **disable_clear_route_cache deprecation**: Replaced by a new `route_cache_action` enum for more granular control

### **New Features:**
1. **route_cache_action enum** (field 18): Provides three modes:
   - `DEFAULT`: Standard behavior (clear when external processor requests)
   - `CLEAR`: Always clear route cache
   - `RETAIN`: Never clear route cache

2. **deferred_close_timeout field** (field 19): For observability mode stream management (default 5 seconds)

3. **Enhanced stream lifecycle management**: New internal classes for managing deferred stream closure in observability mode

## Document Coverage

The 500+ line migration guide includes:

- ✅ Specific proto field names and types with examples
- ✅ Before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- ✅ Explanation of motivation behind changes
- ✅ Cited source files (ext_proc.proto, external_processor.proto, ext_proc.h)
- ✅ Step-by-step migration instructions
- ✅ Testing recommendations and metrics to monitor
- ✅ Rollback procedures
- ✅ Common pitfalls and solutions
- ✅ Backwards compatibility matrix
- ✅ Configuration templates

The guide is written in markdown and saved to `/workspace/documentation.md`, ready for distribution to users planning to upgrade their Envoy deployments.

[#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Specifically, if the\\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\\n118: \\n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\\n120:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\\n121:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\\n122: \\n123:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n124:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n125:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\\n126:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\\n127:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n128:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\\n129: \\n130:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n131:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\\n132:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\\n133:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\\n134:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\\n135:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\\n136: \\n137:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\\n138:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\\n139:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\\n140:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\\n141:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\\n142:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n143:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\\n144:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\\n145:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\\n146:     lte {seconds: 3600}\\n147:     gte {}\\n148:   }];\\n149: \\n150:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n12: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n15: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n16: \n17: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n18: option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n19: option java_multiple_files = true;\n20: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n21: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n22: \n23: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n24: // External Processing Filter\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n26: \n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n28: \n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n31: //\n32: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n33: \n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n36: //\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n41: //\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n44: // and how it should be processed.\n45: //\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n47: //\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n53: //\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\n57: //\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n63: //   to SEND.\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n69: //   request trailers.\n70: //\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n78: //\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n81: //\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n89: //\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n91: // server\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n95: //\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n98: // name.\n99: //\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\n102:   reserved 4;\n103: \n104:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n105: \n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n107:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n109: \n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n113:   // error downstream. (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\\n118:     // to true.\\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\\n120:   }\\n121: \\n122:   reserved 4;\\n123: \\n124:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n125: \\n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\\n127:   // The filter supports both the \\\"Envoy\\\" and \\\"Google\\\" gRPC clients.\\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\\n129: \\n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. There is no\\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n141:   ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n142: \n143:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n144:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n145:   // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n146:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n147:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n148:   repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n149: \n150:   // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n151:   // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n152:   // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n153:   // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n154:   // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n155:   repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n156: \n157:   // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n158:   // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n159:   // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n160:   // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n161:   // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n162:   // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n163:   // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n164:   // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n165:   google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n166:     lte {seconds: 3600}\n167:     gte {}\n168:   }];\n169: \n170:   // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n176:   // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n177:   // with the header prefix set via\n178:   // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n179:   // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n180:   // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n181:   // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. By default, request and response headers are sent,\n27:     // while trailers are skipped.\n28:     DEFAULT = 0;\n29: \n30:     // Send the header or trailer.\n31:     SEND = 1;\n32: \n33:     // Do not send the header or trailer.\n34:     SKIP = 2;\n35:   }\n36: \n37:   // Control how the request and response bodies are handled\n38:   // When body mutation by external processor is enabled, ext_proc filter will always remove\n39:   // the content length header in three cases below because content length can not be guaranteed\n40:   // to be set correctly:\n41:   // 1) STREAMED BodySendMode: header processing completes before body mutation comes back.\n42:   // 2) BUFFERED_PARTIAL BodySendMode: body is buffered and could be injected in different phases.\n43:   // 3) BUFFERED BodySendMode + SKIP HeaderSendMode: header processing (e.g., update content-length) is skipped.\n44:   //\n45:   // In Envoy's http1 codec implementation, removing content length will enable chunked transfer\n46:   // encoding whenever feasible.   "content": "{\"content\":\"1: syntax = \\\"proto3\\\";\\n2: \\n3: package envoy.service.ext_proc.v3;\\n4: \\n5: import \\\"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\\\";\\n6: import \\\"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\\\";\\n7: import \\\"envoy/type/v3/http_status.proto\\\";\\n8: \\n9: import \\\"google/protobuf/duration.proto\\\";\\n10: import \\\"google/protobuf/struct.proto\\\";\\n11: \\n12: import \\\"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\\\";\\n13: import \\\"udpa/annotations/status.proto\\\";\\n14: import \\\"validate/validate.proto\\\";\\n15: \\n16: option java_package = \\\"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\\\";\\n17: option java_outer_classname = \\\"ExternalProcessorProto\\\";\\n18: option java_multiple_files = true;\\n19: option go_package = \\\"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\\\";\\n20: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n21: \\n22: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\\n23: \\n24: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses\\n25: // as part of a filter chain.\\n26: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\\n27: //\\n28: // 1. Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n29: // 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\\n30: //    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\\n31: //    next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\\n33: //    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\\n34: //    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\\n35: // 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\\n36: //    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\\n37: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\\n38: //    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\\n39: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\\n40: //    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\\n41: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\\n42: //    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\\n43: //    was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\\n46: // using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\\n47: // maintain state.\\n48: \\n49: service ExternalProcessor {\\n50:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\\n51:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The actual\\n52:   // protocol is described by the ProcessingRequest and ProcessingResponse\\n53:   // messages below.\\n54:   rpc Process(stream ProcessingRequest) returns (stream ProcessingResponse) {\\n55:   }\\n56: }\\n57: \\n58: // This represents the different types of messages that Envoy can send\\n59: // to an external processing server.\\n60: // [#next-free-field: 11]\\n61: message ProcessingRequest {\\n62:   reserved 1;\\n63: \\n64:   reserved \\\"async_mode\\\";\\n65: \\n66:   // Each request message will include one of the following sub-messages. Which\\n67:   // ones are set for a particular HTTP request/response depend on the\\n68:   // processing mode.\\n69:   oneof request {\\n70:     option (validate.required) = true;\\n71: \\n72:     // Information about the HTTP request headers, as well as peer info and additional\\n73:     // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\\n74:     // HeaderResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\\n75:     HttpHeaders request_headers = 2;\\n76: \\n77:     // Information about the HTTP response headers, as well as peer info and additional\\n78:     // properties. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back a\\n79:     // HeaderResponse message or close the stream.\\n80:     HttpHeaders response_headers = 3;\\n81: \\n82:     // A chunk of the HTTP request body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is true, the server must send back\\n83:     // a BodyResponse message, an ImmediateResponse message, or close the stream.\\n84:     HttpBody request_body = 4;\\n85: \\n86:     // A chunk of the HTTP response body. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back\\n87:     // a BodyResponse message or close the stream.\\n88:     HttpBody response_body = 5;\\n89: \\n90:     // The HTTP trailers for the request path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\\n91:     // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\\n92:     //\\n93:     // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\\n94:     // the original downstream request has trailers.\\n95:     HttpTrailers request_trailers = 6;\\n96: \\n97:     // The HTTP trailers for the response path. Each entry\\n110:   // in the list is populated from the standard\\n111:   // :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>` supported across Envoy.\\n112:   map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 9;\\n113: \\n114:   // Specify whether the filter that sent this request is running in :ref:`observability_mode\\n115:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`\\n116:   // and defaults to false.\\n117:   //\\n118:   // * A value of ``false`` indicates that the server must respond\\n119:   //   to this message by either sending back a matching ProcessingResponse message,\\n120:   //   or by closing the stream.\\n121:   // * A value of ``true`` indicates that the server should not respond to this message, as any\\n122:   //   responses will be ignored. However, it may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages\\n123:   //   are needed.\\n124:   //\\n125:   bool observability_mode = 10;\\n126: }\\n127: \\n128: // For every ProcessingRequest received by the server with the ``observability_mode`` field\\n129: // set to false, the server must send back exactly one ProcessingResponse message.\\n130: // [#next-free-field: 11]\\n131: message ProcessingResponse {\\n132:   oneof response {\\n133:     option (validate.required) = true;\\n134: \\n135:     // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\\n136:     // ``request_headers`` field set.\\n137:     HeadersResponse request_headers = 1;\\n138: \\n139:     // The server must send back this message in response to a message with the\\n140:     // ``response_headers`` field set.\\n141:     HeadersResponse response_headers = 2;\\n142: \\n143:     // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\\n144:     // the ``request_body`` field set.\\n145:     BodyResponse request_body = 3;\\n146: \\n147:     // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\\n148:     // the ``response_body`` field set.\\n149:     BodyResponse response_body = 4;\\n150: \\n151:     // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\\n152:     // the ``request_trailers`` field set.\\n153:     TrailersResponse request_trailers = 5;\\n154: \\n155:     // The server must send back this message in response to a message with\\n156:     // the ``response_trailers`` field set.\\n157:     TrailersResponse response_trailers = 6;\\n158: \\n159:     // If specified, attempt to create a locally generated response, send it\\n160:     // downstream, and stop processing additional filters and ignore any\\n161:     // additional messages received from the remote server for this request or\\n162:     // response. If a response has already started -- for example, if this\\n163:     // message is sent response to a ``response_body`` message -- then\\n164:     // this will either ship the reply directly to the downstream codec,\\n165:     // or reset the stream.\\n166:     ImmediateResponse immediate_response = 7;\\n167:   }\\n168: \\n169:   // Optional metadata that will be emitted as dynamic metadata to be consumed by\\n170:   // following filters. This metadata will be placed in the namespace(s) specified by the top-level\\n171:   // field name(s) of the struct.\\n172:   google.protobuf.Struct dynamic_metadata = 8;\\n173: \\n174:   // Override how parts of the HTTP request and response are processed\\n175:   // for the duration of this particular request/response only. Servers\\n176:   // may use this to intelligently control how requests are processed\\n177:   // based on the headers and other metadata that they see.\\n178:   // This field is only applicable when servers responding to the header requests.\\n179:   // If it is set in the response to the body or trailer requests, it will be ignored by Envoy.\\n180:   // It is also ignored by Envoy when the ext_proc filter config\\n181:   // :ref:`allow_mode_override\\n182:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.allow_mode_override>`\\n183:   // is set to false.\\n184:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode mode_override = 9;\\n185: \\n186:   // When ext_proc server receives a request message, in case it needs more\\n187:   // time to process the message, it sends back a ProcessingResponse message\\n188:   // with a new timeout value. When Envoy receives this response message,\\n189:   // it ignores other fields in the response, just stop the original timer,\\n190:   // which has the timeout value specified in\\n191:   // :ref:`message_timeout\\n192:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\\n193:   // and start a new timer with this ``override_message_timeout`` value and keep the\\n194:   // Envoy ext_proc filter state machine intact.\\n195:   // Has to be >= 1ms and <=\\n196:   // :ref:`max_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.max_message_timeout>`\\n197:   // Such message can be sent at most once in a particular Envoy ext_proc filter processing state.\\n198:   // To enable this API, one has to set ``max_message_timeout`` to a number >= 1ms.\\n199:   google.protobuf.Duration override_message_timeout = 10;\\n200: }\\n201: \\n202: // The following are messages that are sent to the server.\\n203: \\n204: // This message is sent to the external server when the HTTP request and responses\\n205: // are first received.\\n206: message HttpHeaders {\\n207:   // The HTTP request headers. All header keys will be\\n208:   // lower-cased, because HTTP header keys are case-insensitive.\\n209:   // The ``headers`` encoding is based on the runtime guard\\n210:   // envoy_reloadable_features_send_header_raw_value setting.\\n211:   // When it is true, the header value is encoded in the\\n212:   // :ref:`raw_value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.raw_value>` field.\\n213:   // When it is false, the header value is encoded in the\\n214:   // :ref:`value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.value>` field.\\n215:   config.core.v3.HeaderMap headers = 1;\\n216: \\n217:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n218:   // This field is deprecated and not implemented. Attributes will be sent in\\n219:   // the  top-level :ref:`attributes <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest.attributes`\\n220:   // field.\\n221:   map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 2\\n222:       [deprecated = true, (envoy.annotations.deprecated_at_minor_version) = \\\"3.0\\\"];\\n223: \\n224:   // If true, then there is no message body associated with this\\n225:   // request or response.\\n226:   bool end_of_stream = 3;\\n227: }\\n228: \\n229: // This message contains the message body that Envoy sends to the external server.\\n230: message HttpBody {\\n231:   bytes body = 1;\\n232: \\n233:   bool end_of_stream = 2;\\n234: }\\n235: \\n236: // This message contains the trailers.\\n237: message HttpTrailers {\\n238:   // The ``trailers`` encoding is based on the runtime guard\\n239:   // envoy_reloadable_features_send_header_raw_value setting.\\n240:   // When it is true, the header value is encoded in the\\n241:   // :ref:`raw_value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.raw_value>` field.\\n242:   // When it is false, the header value is encoded in the\\n243:   // :ref:`value <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.HeaderValue.value>` field.\\n244:   config.core.v3.HeaderMap trailers = 1;\\n245: }\\n246: \\n247: // The following are messages that may be sent back by the server.\\n248: \\n249: // This message must be sent in response to an HttpHeaders message.\\n250: message HeadersResponse {\\n251:   CommonResponse response = 1;\\n252: }\\n253: \\n254: // This message must be sent in response to an HttpTrailers message.\\n255: message TrailersResponse {\\n256:   // Instructions on how to manipulate the trailers\\n257:   HeaderMutation header_mutation = 1;\\n258: }\\n259: \\n260: // This message must be sent in response to an HttpBody message.\\n261: message BodyResponse {\\n262:   CommonResponse response = 1;\\n263: }\\n264: \\n265: // This message Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n29: // 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\n30: //    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\n31: //    next chunk of the message body.\n32: // 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\n33: //    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\n34: //    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\n35: // 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\n36: //    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\n37: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n38: //    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n39: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n40: //    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n41: // 7. Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\\n29: // 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\\n30: //    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\\n31: //    next chunk of the message body.\\n32: // 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\\n33: //    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\\n34: //    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\\n35: // 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\\n36: //    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\\n37: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\\n38: //    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\\n39: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\\n40: //    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\\n41: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\\n42: //    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\\n43: //    was configured to ignore errors.\\n44: //\\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\\n46: // using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\\n47: // maintain state.\\n48: \\n49: service ExternalProcessor {\\n50:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\\n51:   // give the server control over what the filter does. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server must send back\\n87:     // a BodyResponse message or close the stream.\\n88:     HttpBody response_body = 5;\\n89: \\n90:     // The HTTP trailers for the request path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\\n91:     // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\\n92:     //\\n93:     // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\\n94:     // the original downstream request has trailers.\\n95:     HttpTrailers request_trailers = 6;\\n96: \\n97:     // The HTTP trailers for the response path. Unless ``observability_mode`` is ``true``, the server\\n98:     // must send back a TrailerResponse message or close the stream.\\n99:     //\\n100:     // This message is only sent if the trailers processing mode is set to ``SEND`` and\\n101:     // the original upstream response has trailers.\\n102:     HttpTrailers response_trailers = 7;\\n103:   }\\n104: \\n105:   // Dynamic metadata associated with the request.\\n106:   config.core.v3.Metadata metadata_context = 8;\\n107: \\n108:   // The values of properties selected by the ``request_attributes``\\n109:   // or ``response_attributes`` list in the configuration. Each entry\\n110:   // in the list is populated from the standard\\n111:   // :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>` supported across Envoy.\\n112:   map<string, google.protobuf.Struct> attributes = 9;\\n113: \\n114:   // Specify whether the filter that sent this request is running in :ref:`observability_mode\\n115:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`\\n116:   // and defaults to false.\\n117:   //\\n118:   // * A value of ``false`` indicates that the server must respond\\n119:   //   to this message by either sending back a matching ProcessingResponse message,\\n120:   //   or by closing the stream.\\n121:   // * A value of ``true`` indicates that the server should not respond to this message, as any\\n122:   //   responses will be ignored. Servers\\n176:   // may use this to intelligently control how requests are processed\\n177:   // based on the headers and other metadata that they see.\\n178:   // This field is only applicable when servers responding to the header requests.\\n179:   // If it is set in the response to the body or trailer requests, it will be ignored by Envoy.\\n180:   // It is also ignored by Envoy when the ext_proc filter config\\n181:   // :ref:`allow_mode_override\\n182:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.allow_mode_override>`\\n183:   // is set to false.\\n184:   envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingMode mode_override = 9;\\n185: \\n186:   // When ext_proc server receives a request message, in case it needs more\\n187:   // time to process the message, it sends back a ProcessingResponse message\\n188:   // with a new timeout value. server.\\n248: \\n249: // This message must be sent in response to an HttpHeaders message.\\n250: message HeadersResponse {\\n251:   CommonResponse response = 1;\\n252: }\\n253: \\n254: // This contains common fields between header and body responses.\\n266: // [#next-free-field: 6]\\n267: message CommonResponse {\\n268:   enum ResponseStatus {\\n269:     // Apply the mutation instructions in this message to the\\n270:     // request or response, and then continue processing the filter\\n271:     // stream as normal. When Envoy receives this response message,\n189:   // it ignores other fields in the response, just stop the original timer,\n190:   // which has the timeout value specified in\n191:   // :ref:`message_timeout\n192:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n193:   // and start a new timer with this ``override_message_timeout`` value and keep the\n194:   // Envoy ext_proc filter state machine intact.\n195:   // Has to be >= 1ms and <=\n196:   // :ref:`max_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.max_message_timeout>`\n197:   // Such message can be sent at most once in a particular Envoy ext_proc filter processing state.\n198:   // To enable this API, one has to set ``max_message_timeout`` to a number >= 1ms.\n199:   google.protobuf.Duration override_message_timeout = 10;\n200: }\n201: \n202: // The following are messages that are sent to the server.\n203: \n204: // This message is sent to the external server when the HTTP request and responses\n205: // are first received.\n206: message HttpHeaders {\n207:   // The HTTP request headers. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. The :ref:`stat prefix\\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\\n37: \\n38: The following statistics are supported:\\n39: \\n40: .. csv-table::\\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\\n42:   :widths: auto\\n43: \\n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\\n55: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--7b8baff1@7d6a8ad71741583b3a75f94937b6f294b39e2667/-/blob/docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst\"}",
  "structuredContent": {
    "content": "1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n30: \n31: Statistics\n32: ----------\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n37: \n38: The following statistics are supported:\n39: \n40: .. csv-table::\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\n42:   :widths: auto\n43: \n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n55: ",
